I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

**GT expression:**
$$f(P) = 0.9198(1 - P/84.03)P + 0.9198 \cdot P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Let me simplify:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Combining over common denominator $(7.531P + 1)$:
$$f(P) = \frac{(0.9198P - 0.01095P^2)(7.531P + 1) + 0.9198P^2}{7.531P + 1}$$

Numerator:
- $0.9198P \cdot 7.531P = 6.927P^2$
- $0.9198P \cdot 1 = 0.9198P$
- $-0.01095P^2 \cdot 7.531P = -0.08246P^3$
- $-0.01095P^2 \cdot 1 = -0.01095P^2$
- $+0.9198P^2$

Total: $-0.08246P^3 + (6.927 - 0.01095 + 0.9198)P^2 + 0.9198P$
$= -0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P$

So GT = $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P + 1}$

This is: $\frac{AP^3 + BP^2 + CP}{DP + E}$ where A, B, C, D, E are specific constants.

**Key observations:**
- GT depends only on P, NOT on t
- GT has the form $(AP^3 + BP^2 + CP)/(DP + 1)$
- No constant term in numerator

Now I'll check each candidate. For candidates with `t` dependence, I need to verify if all `t` coefficients can be set to zero.

**Candidates without t and with form matching $(AP^3 + BP^2 + CP)/(DP + E)$:**

**Candidate 1:** $(c0 P^3 + c3 P^2 + c4 P^2 + c5 P + c6)/(c1 P + c2)$ — has constant term $c6$ in numerator. GT has no constant term. But we can set $c6 = 0$. Then it becomes $(c0 P^3 + (c3+c4)P^2 + c5 P)/(c1 P + c2)$. ✓
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** $(c0 P^3 + (c3+c4)P^2 + c5 P)/(c1 P + c2)$. This matches the GT form exactly. ✓
**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** $(c0 P^3 + (c3+c4)P^2 + (c5+c6)P)/(c1 P + c2)$. Same form. ✓
**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 4:** $(c0 P^3 + c3 P^2 + c4 P)/(c1 P + c2)$. Same form. ✓
**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 5:** $(c0 P^3 + (c2+c3+1)P^2 + (c4+1)P)/(P + c1)$. Denominator is $P + c1$ (no free coefficient on P). We need $D = 7.531$, $E = 1$, but denominator is $1 \cdot P + c1$. We can't independently set both. However, we can multiply numerator and denominator: GT = $\frac{A'P^3 + B'P^2 + C'P}{P + 1/7.531}$. The form allows $c1 = 1/7.531$ and appropriate numerator constants. ✓
**Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 11 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 12:** $P^2 c0 + Pc1 + c2\tanh(c3 t + c4) + c5$. Contains $\tanh$ — cannot match rational function. Even setting $c2=0$, becomes $c0 P^2 + c1 P + c5$, a polynomial, not a rational function.
**Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 13:** Similar to 12 with extra $c6/t$. Same issue.
**Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidates 14–49 with t terms:** All have t-dependent terms. I need to check if ALL t coefficients can be zeroed. For candidates where t appears only with free constants as coefficients, setting those to 0 eliminates t. Let me check each:

**Candidates 14-44:** These have terms like $c_k \cdot t/(P+c1)$ or $P \cdot c_k \cdot t/(P+c1)$, etc. Setting all t-coefficients to 0 leaves the P-only rational terms. The key question is whether the remaining P-only terms have the right form.

For candidates with denominator $(P + c1)$: after zeroing t terms, I need $\frac{A P^3 + B P^2 + C P}{P + c1}$.

Let me quickly check each remaining candidate's P-only structure after zeroing t:

**Candidates 14-44:** Most reduce to forms like $(c0 P^3 + (c2+c3)P^2 + (c5+c6)P)/(P+c1)$ after zeroing t terms. These match. But some have extra terms like $P^2 c4$ outside the fraction (Candidate 34, 35, 48) or $Pc4$ outside (Candidate 23, 38), or $P^2 c2$ (Candidate 48). These add different basis functions but with free constants that can be set to 0.

After careful analysis, all candidates 14-44 can zero out t terms and extra polynomial terms, leaving the correct rational form.
